# Architecture Q&A: Envoy HTTP Filter Chain

**Repository:** envoyproxy/envoy
**Task Type:** Architecture Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Envoy is a high-performance service proxy that processes HTTP requests through a layered filter architecture. Understanding how a request flows from initial TCP accept through to the upstream server is fundamental to working with Envoy's codebase.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Envoy's HTTP request processing pipeline:

### Q1: Listener to Connection Manager

When a downstream client opens a TCP connection to Envoy, how does the listener hand off the connection to the HTTP connection manager? Specifically:
- What mechanism selects which network filter chain to use for an incoming connection?
- How is the HTTP connection manager (`ConnectionManagerImpl`) installed as a network filter?
- What happens in `onData()` when the first bytes arrive?

### Q2: HTTP Filter Chain Creation and Iteration

Once HTTP request headers are parsed, how does Envoy build and iterate through the HTTP filter chain?
- At what point in request processing is the HTTP filter chain created?
- In what order are decoder filters invoked vs. encoder filters?
- What return values can a filter use to control iteration (stop, continue, buffer)?

### Q3: Router and Upstream

How does the router filter (the terminal HTTP filter) forward requests to upstream servers?
- How does the router obtain the target cluster and select a specific upstream host?
- What is the role of `UpstreamRequest` and the upstream filter chain?
- How does the response flow back through the filter chain to the downstream client?

### Q4: Architectural Boundaries

Explain the distinction between these two "filter chain" concepts in Envoy:
- The network-level filter chain (managed by `FilterChainManager`)
- The HTTP-level filter chain (managed by `FilterManager`)

Why are they separate, and how do they relate to each other?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:

{"content":"42: /* The Upstream request is the base class for forwarding HTTP upstream.\n43:  *\n44:  * On the new request path, payload (headers/body/metadata/data) still arrives via\n45:  * the accept[X]fromRouter functions. Said data is immediately passed off to the\n46:  * UpstreamFilterManager, which passes each item through the filter chain until\n47:  * it arrives at the last filter in the chain, the UpstreamCodecFilter. If the upstream\n48:  * stream is not established, the UpstreamCodecFilter returns StopAllIteration, and the\n49:  * FilterManager will buffer data, using watermarks to push back to the router\n50:  * filter if buffers become overrun. When an upstream connection is established,\n51:  * the UpstreamCodecFilter will send data upstream.\n52:  *\n53:  * On the new response path, payload arrives from upstream via the UpstreamCodecFilter's\n54:  * CodecBridge. The investigation is complete. The report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` covering all four questions:

**Q1 — Listener to Connection Manager**: Traces the path from `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` through `FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()` (multi-level matching on destination port/IP, SNI, transport/application protocol), to `createNetworkFilterChain()` which installs the HCM as a `Network::ReadFilter` via its factory in `config.cc:329`. The HCM's `onData()` creates the HTTP codec on first call and dispatches bytes through `codec_->dispatch()`.

**Q2 — HTTP Filter Chain Creation and Iteration**: The HTTP filter chain is created in `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` at line 1531 via `filter_manager_.createDownstreamFilterChain()`, after headers are parsed and the route is resolved. Decoder filters run in FIFO order, encoder filters in LIFO (reverse). Filters control iteration via `FilterHeadersStatus` (Continue, StopIteration, StopAllIterationAndBuffer, StopAllIterationAndWatermark, ContinueAndDontEndStream) and analogous `FilterDataStatus`/`FilterTrailersStatus` enums.

**Q3 — Router and Upstream**: The router obtains the cluster via `ClusterManager::getThreadLocalCluster()`, selects a host via `cluster->chooseHost()`, creates a `GenericConnPool`, then constructs an `UpstreamRequest` with its own `UpstreamFilterManager`. The upstream filter chain terminates at `UpstreamCodecFilter`. Responses flow back through the upstream filter chain, then via `Filter::onUpstreamHeaders()` which calls `callbacks_->encodeHeaders()`, triggering reverse encoder filter iteration on the downstream `FilterManager`.

**Q4 — Architectural Boundaries**: Network filter chains (per-connection, raw bytes, managed by `Network::FilterChainManager` + `Network::F

  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Architecture\n\n## Q1: Listener to Connection Manager\n\n### Filter Chain Selection\n\nWhen a downstream client opens a TCP connection, the listener first runs **listener filters** (e.g., TLS Inspector, HTTP Inspector) to populate connection metadata such as SNI, ALPN, and detected protocol. Once listener filters complete, `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` (`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:27`) is called.\n\nThis method invokes `FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()` (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.cc:542`) to select the appropriate network filter chain. The selection algorithm is a multi-level matching hierarchy:\n\n1. **Destination port** \u2014 matches on the local port (or catch-all port 0)\n2. **Destination IP** \u2014 matches on the local IP address via `findFilterChainForDestinationIP()` using a `LcTrie` for CIDR matching (`:591`)\n3. **Server name (SNI)** \u2014 matches on exact server name, wildcard domains, or catch-all via `findFilterChainForServerName()` (`:608`)\n4. **Transport protocol** \u2014 matches on detected transport protocol (e.g., `\"tls\"`) via `findFilterChainForTransportProtocol()` (`:639`)\n5. **Application protocol (ALPN)** \u2014 matches on application protocols via `findFilterChainForApplicationProtocols()`\n\nAlternatively, if a `matcher_` is configured (xDS filter chain matching), `findFilterChainUsingMatcher()` (`:577`) uses the Unified Matcher Framework instead.\n\nIf no filter chain matches, the connection is closed with `no_filter_chain_match` (`active_stream_listener_base.cc:31-40`). If a default filter chain is configured, it serves as fallback.\n\n### Installing the HTTP Connection Manager\n\nAfter selecting a `Network::FilterChain`, `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` calls `config_->filterChainFactory().createNetworkFilterChain()` (`active_stream_listener_base.cc:56`), which delegates to `ListenerImpl::createNetworkFilterChain()` (`source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.cc:959`). This calls `Configuration::FilterChainUtility::buildFilterChain()`, which iterates through the `networkFilterFactories()` list from the selected `FilterChain` and invokes each factory callback.\n\nFor HTTP traffic, one of these factory callbacks is produced by `HttpConnectionManagerFilterConfigFactory::createFilterFactoryFromProtoAndHopByHop()` (`source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc:297`). This factory returns a lambda that:\n\n1. Creates a `ConnectionManagerImpl` instance (`config.cc:321`)\n2. Adds it as a read filter to the `Network::FilterManager` via `filter_manager.addReadFilter(std::move(hcm))` (`config.cc:329`)\n\nThe `ConnectionManagerImpl` class (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h:60`) implements `Network::ReadFilter`, making it a network-level read filter.\n\n### What Happens in `onData()`\n\nWhen the first bytes arrive from the downstream connection, the network-level `FilterManagerImpl::onRead()` (`source/common/network/filter_manager_impl.cc:100`) calls `onContinueReading()` (`:62`), which iterates through registered read filters, calling `onData()` on each.\n\nFor the HCM, `ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()` (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:505`) executes:\n\n1. **Codec creation** \u2014 If no codec exists yet, `createCodec(data)` (`:515`) is called, which uses `config_->createCodec()` (`:486`) to auto-detect the protocol (HTTP/1.1 or HTTP/2) based on the initial bytes and create the appropriate codec (`Http1::ServerConnectionImpl` or `Http2::ServerConnectionImpl`).\n2. **Dispatching** \u2014 The codec's `dispatch(data)` method (`:522`) is called in a loop. The codec parses HTTP frames and calls back into the HCM via the `ServerConnectionCallbacks` interface (e.g., `newStream()` when a new request starts, then `decodeHeaders()`/`decodeData()` on the stream).\n3. **Error handling** \u2014 Buffer floods, protocol errors, and overload conditions are caught and result in connection closure.\n4. **HTTP/1.1 redispatch** \u2014 For HTTP/1.1, if there is remaining data after a complete message and no active streams, the loop redispatches (`:545-549`).\n\nFor HTTP/3 (QUIC), `onNewConnection()` (`:560`) is called instead because QUIC handles de-multiplexing internally. The codec is created with a dummy buffer, and `onData()` is never called.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: HTTP Filter Chain Creation and Iteration\n\n### When the HTTP Filter Chain Is Created\n\nThe HTTP filter chain is created **after request headers are fully parsed** but **before they are dispatched to filters**. The sequence is:\n\n1. The codec parses a complete set of request headers and calls `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:400`), which creates an `ActiveStream` (`:420`) and returns it as the `RequestDecoder`.\n2. The codec then calls `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` (`conn_manager_impl.cc:1321`) with the parsed headers.\n3. Inside `decodeHeaders()`, after header validation, route resolution (`refreshCachedRoute()` at `:1520`), and request mutation, the filter chain is created by calling `filter_manager_.createDownstreamFilterChain()` (`:1531`).\n4. `DownstreamFilterManager::createDownstreamFilterChain()` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:1125`) delegates to `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` (`:1695`).\n5. `createFilterChain()` calls `filter_chain_factory.createFilterChain(callbacks)` (`:1734`), where the `FilterChainFactory` (configured by the HCM) invokes each HTTP filter factory in order. Each factory calls `callbacks.addStreamDecoderFilter()`, `addStreamEncoderFilter()`, or `addStreamFilter()` to register the filter.\n6. After chain creation, `filter_manager_.decodeHeaders()` (`:1567`) is called to start iteration.\n\n### Decoder vs. Encoder Filter Ordering\n\n- **Decoder filters** (request path) are invoked in **FIFO order** \u2014 the first filter added is called first. They process: `decodeHeaders()` -> `decodeData()` -> `decodeTrailers()`.\n- **Encoder filters** (response path) are invoked in **reverse order** (LIFO) \u2014 the last filter added is called first. They process: `encodeHeaders()` -> `encodeData()` -> `encodeTrailers()`.\n\nThis is implemented through the `FilterManager` which maintains two separate lists: `decoder_filters_` and `encoder_filters_` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.h`). Decoder iteration uses `commonDecodePrefix()` starting from the beginning, while encoder iteration uses `commonEncodePrefix()` starting from the end.\n\nIn `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` (`filter_manager.cc:574`), iteration proceeds forward through `decoder_filters_` (`:584`), calling `(*entry)->decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` on each filter (`:592`).\n\nIn `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` (`filter_manager.cc:1260`), iteration proceeds through `encoder_filters_` via `commonEncodePrefix()` (`:1269`), calling `(*entry)->handle_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` (`:1281`).\n\n### Return Values for Iteration Control\n\nFilters control iteration via return status enums defined in `envoy/http/filter.h`:\n\n**`FilterHeadersStatus`** (`:38`):\n- **`Continue`** \u2014 Continue to the next filter in the chain.\n- **`StopIteration`** \u2014 Stop iterating for headers; `continueDecoding()`/`continueEncoding()` must be called later to resume.\n- **`ContinueAndDontEndStream`** \u2014 Continue headers iteration but delay `end_stream`, allowing the filter to inject a body later.\n- **`StopAllIterationAndBuffer`** \u2014 Stop all iteration (headers, data, trailers) and buffer incoming body data. Triggers 413/500 if buffer limits are exceeded.\n- **`StopAllIterationAndWatermark`** \u2014 Same as above but applies flow control watermarks to cease incoming data flow.\n\n**`FilterDataStatus`** (`:129`):\n- **`Continue`** \u2014 Continue to next filter, sending any buffered data.\n- **`StopIterationAndBuffer`** \u2014 Stop and buffer data.\n- **`StopIterationAndWatermark`** \u2014 Stop, buffer, and apply watermarks.\n- **`StopIterationNoBuffer`** \u2014 Stop without buffering (data is discarded).\n\n**`FilterTrailersStatus`** (`:171`):\n- **`Continue`** \u2014 Continue to next filter.\n- **`StopIteration`** \u2014 Stop; `continueDecoding()`/`continueEncoding()` required to resume.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Router and Upstream\n\n### Cluster Selection and Host Selection\n\nThe **router filter** (`source/common/router/router.h`, `source/common/router/router.cc`) is the terminal HTTP filter in the downstream filter chain. Its `decodeHeaders()` method:\n\n1. **Resolves the route** \u2014 The route was already resolved in `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` via `refreshCachedRoute()`. The router accesses it via `callbacks_->route()` and extracts the `RouteEntry` (`router.cc:518`).\n2. **Gets the cluster** \u2014 Calls `config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName())` (`:524`) to get the `ThreadLocalCluster` for the target cluster name from the `ClusterManager`.\n3. **Selects a host** \u2014 Calls `cluster->chooseHost(this)` (`:700`), where `this` (the `Filter`) implements `LoadBalancerContext`. The cluster's load balancer uses the context (priority, hash, metadata, etc.) to select a specific upstream `Host`.\n4. **Creates a connection pool** \u2014 `continueDecodeHeaders()` (`:749`) calls `createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host)` (`:756`), which returns a `GenericConnPool` representing an HTTP connection pool to the selected host.\n\n### `UpstreamRequest` and the Upstream Filter Chain\n\nAfter obtaining a connection pool, the router creates an `UpstreamRequest` (`router.cc:842`):\n\n```\nUpstreamRequestPtr upstream_request = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(\n    *this, std::move(generic_conn_pool), ...);\n```\n\nThe `UpstreamRequest` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.h:67`) manages the lifecycle of a single upstream attempt. It:\n\n- Implements `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks` \u2014 receives `onPoolReady()` when a connection is available and `onPoolFailure()` on failure.\n- Contains an `UpstreamFilterManager` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.cc:158`) \u2014 a specialized version of `Http::FilterManager` that manages upstream HTTP filters.\n- Contains an `UpstreamRequestFilterManagerCallbacks` \u2014 bridges the upstream filter chain back to the `UpstreamRequest`.\n\nAs documented in the class header comment (`upstream_request.h:42-66`):\n\n**Request path**: Data arrives via `acceptHeadersFromRouter()`, `acceptDataFromRouter()`, `acceptTrailersFromRouter()`. This data is passed to the `UpstreamFilterManager`, which runs it through the upstream filter chain. The last filter is the `UpstreamCodecFilter`, which sends data to the upstream server. If the upstream connection is not yet established, `UpstreamCodecFilter` returns `StopAllIteration`, and the `FilterManager` buffers data.\n\n**Response path**: Upstream responses arrive via the `UpstreamCodecFilter`'s `CodecBridge`, are passed through the upstream filter chain in reverse, and emerge via `UpstreamRequestFilterManagerCallbacks`'s `encode[X]()` functions, which call `UpstreamRequest::decode[X]()` (legacy naming), which finally call `RouterFilterInterface::onUpstream[X]()` on the router filter.\n\n### Response Flow Back to Downstream\n\nWhen the router filter receives upstream response headers via `Filter::onUpstreamHeaders()` (`router.cc:1702`):\n\n1. It performs outlier detection, retry logic, and internal redirect checks.\n2. If the response is accepted (no retry needed), it calls `callbacks_->encodeHeaders(std::move(headers), end_stream, ...)` (`:1878`).\n3. This triggers `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` on the downstream `FilterManager`, which iterates through encoder filters in **reverse order** (`:1260`).\n4. After all encoder filters run, `filter_manager_callbacks_.encodeHeaders()` (`:1340`) is called, which reaches `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders()` \u2014 this writes the response headers to the downstream codec's `ResponseEncoder`.\n5. Similarly, `onUpstreamData()` calls `callbacks_->encodeData()` (`:1903`), and `onUpstreamTrailers()` calls `callbacks_->encodeTrailers()`.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: Architectural Boundaries\n\n### Network-Level Filter Chain (`FilterChainManager`)\n\nThe **network-level filter chain** operates at the TCP connection level and is managed by two cooperating components:\n\n- **`Network::FilterChainManager`** (`envoy/network/filter.h:681`) \u2014 Selects which `Network::FilterChain` to use for a given connection based on connection properties (destination IP/port, SNI, ALPN, transport protocol). Implemented by `FilterChainManagerImpl` (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h:172`).\n- **`Network::FilterManager`** (`envoy/network/filter.h:296`) \u2014 Manages the actual list of `ReadFilter`/`WriteFilter`/`Filter` instances installed on a single connection. Implemented by `FilterManagerImpl` (`source/common/network/filter_manager_impl.h`).\n\nKey characteristics:\n- **One instance per listener** for `FilterChainManager` (selects chain configuration).\n- **One instance per connection** for `FilterManager` (manages the active filter pipeline).\n- Network filters see raw bytes (`Buffer::Instance`), not HTTP semantics.\n- Read filters are invoked in **FIFO** order; write filters in **LIFO** order (`envoy/network/filter.h:301-316`).\n- Filters return `Network::FilterStatus::Continue` or `StopIteration`.\n- Examples: TCP proxy, rate limit, RBAC, and critically, the **HTTP connection manager**.\n\n### HTTP-Level Filter Chain (`Http::FilterManager`)\n\nThe **HTTP-level filter chain** operates at the HTTP request/response level and is managed by:\n\n- **`Http::FilterManager`** (`source/common/http/filter_manager.h:679`) \u2014 Manages per-stream decoder and encoder filter chains. Each HTTP stream (request/response pair) gets its own `FilterManager` instance.\n- **`Http::FilterChainFactory`** (interface, not a file \u2014 used via `ConnectionManagerConfig`) \u2014 Creates the HTTP filter chain for each stream by invoking configured filter factories.\n\nKey characteristics:\n- **One instance per HTTP stream** (not per connection \u2014 a single HTTP/2 connection can have many concurrent streams, each with its own `FilterManager`).\n- HTTP filters see parsed HTTP semantics: `RequestHeaderMap`, `ResponseHeaderMap`, `Buffer::Instance` (for body), `TrailerMap`.\n- Decoder filters (request path) are invoked in **FIFO** order; encoder filters (response path) in **LIFO** order.\n- Filters return rich status enums (`FilterHeadersStatus`, `FilterDataStatus`, `FilterTrailersStatus`) with buffering and watermark control.\n- The terminal decoder filter is typically the **router filter**, which forwards requests upstream.\n\n### Why They Are Separate\n\nThe two filter chain levels exist because they operate at fundamentally different abstraction levels:\n\n1. **Scope and multiplexing**: A network filter chain is per-connection and handles raw byte streams. For HTTP/2 and HTTP/3, a single connection carries multiple concurrent streams. The HTTP filter chain is per-stream, allowing independent processing of each request/response pair within a multiplexed connection.\n\n2. **Protocol independence**: Network filters are protocol-agnostic. The same listener can handle TCP proxy traffic (no HTTP parsing) or HTTP traffic depending on which network filters are configured. The HTTP connection manager is itself a network filter that bridges the two levels.\n\n3. **Configuration flexibility**: Network-level filter chain selection uses connection properties available before any data is read (destination IP, SNI from TLS ClientHello, etc.). HTTP-level processing uses request-level properties (headers, routes, etc.) that are only available after HTTP parsing.\n\n### How They Relate\n\nThe relationship is hierarchical:\n\n```\nListener\n  -> FilterChainManager selects a Network::FilterChain (per connection)\n    -> Network::FilterManager runs network filters (per connection)\n      -> ConnectionManagerImpl (a network ReadFilter)\n        -> Codec parses HTTP frames\n          -> ActiveStream created (per HTTP stream)\n            -> Http::FilterManager runs HTTP filters (per stream)\n              -> Router filter (terminal) sends to upstream\n```\n\nThe `ConnectionManagerImpl` serves as the bridge: it is a `Network::ReadFilter` in the network filter chain, and it owns the HTTP codec and creates `Http::FilterManager` instances for each stream. Its `onData()` method receives raw bytes from the network filter pipeline, passes them to the HTTP codec for parsing, and the codec triggers HTTP-level processing through `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()`/`decodeData()`, which delegates to the per-stream `Http::FilterManager`.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Files and Classes\n\n| Component | File | Class/Function Once listener filters complete, `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` (`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:27`) is called.\n\nThis method invokes `FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()` (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.cc:542`) to select the appropriate network filter chain. The selection algorithm is a multi-level matching hierarchy:\n\n1. **Destination port** \u2014 matches on the local port (or catch-all port 0)\n2. **Destination IP** \u2014 matches on the local IP address via `findFilterChainForDestinationIP()` using a `LcTrie` for CIDR matching (`:591`)\n3. **Server name (SNI)** \u2014 matches on exact server name, wildcard domains, or catch-all via `findFilterChainForServerName()` (`:608`)\n4. **Transport protocol** \u2014 matches on detected transport protocol (e.g., `\"tls\"`) via `findFilterChainForTransportProtocol()` (`:639`)\n5. **Application protocol (ALPN)** \u2014 matches on application protocols via `findFilterChainForApplicationProtocols()`\n\nAlternatively, if a `matcher_` is configured (xDS filter chain matching), `findFilterChainUsingMatcher()` (`:577`) uses the Unified Matcher Framework instead.\n\nIf no filter chain matches, the connection is closed with `no_filter_chain_match` (`active_stream_listener_base.cc:31-40`). The codec parses HTTP frames and calls back into the HCM via the `ServerConnectionCallbacks` interface (e.g., `newStream()` when a new request starts, then `decodeHeaders()`/`decodeData()` on the stream).\n3. **Error handling** \u2014 Buffer floods, protocol errors, and overload conditions are caught and result in connection closure.\n4. **HTTP/1.1 redispatch** \u2014 For HTTP/1.1, if there is remaining data after a complete message and no active streams, the loop redispatches (`:545-549`).\n\nFor HTTP/3 (QUIC), `onNewConnection()` (`:560`) is called instead because QUIC handles de-multiplexing internally. The codec is created with a dummy buffer, and `onData()` is never called.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: HTTP Filter Chain Creation and Iteration\n\n### When the HTTP Filter Chain Is Created\n\nThe HTTP filter chain is created **after request headers are fully parsed** but **before they are dispatched to filters**. The sequence is:\n\n1. The codec parses a complete set of request headers and calls `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:400`), which creates an `ActiveStream` (`:420`) and returns it as the `RequestDecoder`.\n2. The codec then calls `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` (`conn_manager_impl.cc:1321`) with the parsed headers.\n3. Inside `decodeHeaders()`, after header validation, route resolution (`refreshCachedRoute()` at `:1520`), and request mutation, the filter chain is created by calling `filter_manager_.createDownstreamFilterChain()` (`:1531`).\n4. `DownstreamFilterManager::createDownstreamFilterChain()` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:1125`) delegates to `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` (`:1695`).\n5. `createFilterChain()` calls `filter_chain_factory.createFilterChain(callbacks)` (`:1734`), where the `FilterChainFactory` (configured by the HCM) invokes each HTTP filter factory in order. Each factory calls `callbacks.addStreamDecoderFilter()`, `addStreamEncoderFilter()`, or `addStreamFilter()` to register the filter.\n6. After chain creation, `filter_manager_.decodeHeaders()` (`:1567`) is called to start iteration.\n\n### Decoder vs. Encoder Filter Ordering\n\n- **Decoder filters** (request path) are invoked in **FIFO order** \u2014 the first filter added is called first. They process: `decodeHeaders()` -> `decodeData()` -> `decodeTrailers()`.\n- **Encoder filters** (response path) are invoked in **reverse order** (LIFO) \u2014 the last filter added is called first. They process: `encodeHeaders()` -> `encodeData()` -> `encodeTrailers()`.\n\nThis is implemented through the `FilterManager` which maintains two separate lists: `decoder_filters_` and `encoder_filters_` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.h`). Decoder iteration uses `commonDecodePrefix()` starting from the beginning, while encoder iteration uses `commonEncodePrefix()` starting from the end.\n\nIn `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` (`filter_manager.cc:574`), iteration proceeds forward through `decoder_filters_` (`:584`), calling `(*entry)->decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` on each filter (`:592`).\n\nIn `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` (`filter_manager.cc:1260`), iteration proceeds through `encoder_filters_` via `commonEncodePrefix()` (`:1269`), calling `(*entry)->handle_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` (`:1281`).\n\n### Return Values for Iteration Control\n\nFilters control iteration via return status enums defined in `envoy/http/filter.h`:\n\n**`FilterHeadersStatus`** (`:38`):\n- **`Continue`** \u2014 Continue to the next filter in the chain.\n- **`StopIteration`** \u2014 Stop iterating for headers; `continueDecoding()`/`continueEncoding()` must be called later to resume.\n- **`ContinueAndDontEndStream`** \u2014 Continue headers iteration but delay `end_stream`, allowing the filter to inject a body later.\n- **`StopAllIterationAndBuffer`** \u2014 Stop all iteration (headers, data, trailers) and buffer incoming body data. Triggers 413/500 if buffer limits are exceeded.\n- **`StopAllIterationAndWatermark`** \u2014 Same as above but applies flow control watermarks to cease incoming data flow.\n\n**`FilterDataStatus`** (`:129`):\n- **`Continue`** \u2014 Continue to next filter, sending any buffered data.\n- **`StopIterationAndBuffer`** \u2014 Stop and buffer data.\n- **`StopIterationAndWatermark`** \u2014 Stop, buffer, and apply watermarks.\n- **`StopIterationNoBuffer`** \u2014 Stop without buffering (data is discarded).\n\n**`FilterTrailersStatus`** (`:171`):\n- **`Continue`** \u2014 Continue to next filter.\n- **`StopIteration`** \u2014 Stop; `continueDecoding()`/`continueEncoding()` required to resume.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Router and Upstream\n\n### Cluster Selection and Host Selection\n\nThe **router filter** (`source/common/router/router.h`, `source/common/router/router.cc`) is the terminal HTTP filter in the downstream filter chain. Its `decodeHeaders()` method:\n\n1. **Resolves the route** \u2014 The route was already resolved in `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` via `refreshCachedRoute()`. The router accesses it via `callbacks_->route()` and extracts the `RouteEntry` (`router.cc:518`).\n2. **Gets the cluster** \u2014 Calls `config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName())` (`:524`) to get the `ThreadLocalCluster` for the target cluster name from the `ClusterManager`.\n3. **Selects a host** \u2014 Calls `cluster->chooseHost(this)` (`:700`), where `this` (the `Filter`) implements `LoadBalancerContext`. The cluster's load balancer uses the context (priority, hash, metadata, etc.) to select a specific upstream `Host`.\n4. **Creates a connection pool** \u2014 `continueDecodeHeaders()` (`:749`) calls `createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host)` (`:756`), which returns a `GenericConnPool` representing an HTTP connection pool to the selected host.\n\n### `UpstreamRequest` and the Upstream Filter Chain\n\nAfter obtaining a connection pool, the router creates an `UpstreamRequest` (`router.cc:842`):\n\n```\nUpstreamRequestPtr upstream_request = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(\n    *this, std::move(generic_conn_pool), ...);\n```\n\nThe `UpstreamRequest` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.h:67`) manages the lifecycle of a single upstream attempt. It:\n\n- Implements `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks` \u2014 receives `onPoolReady()` when a connection is available and `onPoolFailure()` on failure.\n- Contains an `UpstreamFilterManager` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.cc:158`) \u2014 a specialized version of `Http::FilterManager` that manages upstream HTTP filters.\n- Contains an `UpstreamRequestFilterManagerCallbacks` \u2014 bridges the upstream filter chain back to the `UpstreamRequest`.\n\nAs documented in the class header comment (`upstream_request.h:42-66`):\n\n**Request path**: Data arrives via `acceptHeadersFromRouter()`, `acceptDataFromRouter()`, `acceptTrailersFromRouter()`. This data is passed to the `UpstreamFilterManager`, which runs it through the upstream filter chain. The last filter is the `UpstreamCodecFilter`, which sends data to the upstream server. If the upstream connection is not yet established, `UpstreamCodecFilter` returns `StopAllIteration`, and the `FilterManager` buffers data.\n\n**Response path**: Upstream responses arrive via the `UpstreamCodecFilter`'s `CodecBridge`, are passed through the upstream filter chain in reverse, and emerge via `UpstreamRequestFilterManagerCallbacks`'s `encode[X]()` functions, which call `UpstreamRequest::decode[X]()` (legacy naming), which finally call `RouterFilterInterface::onUpstream[X]()` on the router filter.\n\n### Response Flow Back to Downstream\n\nWhen the router filter receives upstream response headers via `Filter::onUpstreamHeaders()` (`router.cc:1702`):\n\n1. It performs outlier detection, retry logic, and internal redirect checks.\n2. If the response is accepted (no retry needed), it calls `callbacks_->encodeHeaders(std::move(headers), end_stream, ...)` (`:1878`).\n3. This triggers `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` on the downstream `FilterManager`, which iterates through encoder filters in **reverse order** (`:1260`).\n4. After all encoder filters run, `filter_manager_callbacks_.encodeHeaders()` (`:1340`) is called, which reaches `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders()` \u2014 this writes the response headers to the downstream codec's `ResponseEncoder`.\n5. Similarly, `onUpstreamData()` calls `callbacks_->encodeData()` (`:1903`), and `onUpstreamTrailers()` calls `callbacks_->encodeTrailers()`.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: Architectural Boundaries\n\n### Network-Level Filter Chain (`FilterChainManager`)\n\nThe **network-level filter chain** operates at the TCP connection level and is managed by two cooperating components:\n\n- **`Network::FilterChainManager`** (`envoy/network/filter.h:681`) \u2014 Selects which `Network::FilterChain` to use for a given connection based on connection properties (destination IP/port, SNI, ALPN, transport protocol). Implemented by `FilterChainManagerImpl` (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h:172`).\n- **`Network::FilterManager`** (`envoy/network/filter.h:296`) \u2014 Manages the actual list of `ReadFilter`/`WriteFilter`/`Filter` instances installed on a single connection. Implemented by `FilterManagerImpl` (`source/common/network/filter_manager_impl.h`).\n\nKey characteristics:\n- **One instance per listener** for `FilterChainManager` (selects chain configuration).\n- **One instance per connection** for `FilterManager` (manages the active filter pipeline).\n- Network filters see raw bytes (`Buffer::Instance`), not HTTP semantics.\n- Read filters are invoked in **FIFO** order; write filters in **LIFO** order (`envoy/network/filter.h:301-316`).\n- Filters return `Network::FilterStatus::Continue` or `StopIteration`.\n- Examples: TCP proxy, rate limit, RBAC, and critically, the **HTTP connection manager**.\n\n### HTTP-Level Filter Chain (`Http::FilterManager`)\n\nThe **HTTP-level filter chain** operates at the HTTP request/response level and is managed by:\n\n- **`Http::FilterManager`** (`source/common/http/filter_manager.h:679`) \u2014 Manages per-stream decoder and encoder filter chains. Each HTTP stream (request/response pair) gets its own `FilterManager` instance.\n- **`Http::FilterChainFactory`** (interface, not a file \u2014 used via `ConnectionManagerConfig`) \u2014 Creates the HTTP filter chain for each stream by invoking configured filter factories.\n\nKey characteristics:\n- **One instance per HTTP stream** (not per connection \u2014 a single HTTP/2 connection can have many concurrent streams, each with its own `FilterManager`).\n- HTTP filters see parsed HTTP semantics: `RequestHeaderMap`, `ResponseHeaderMap`, `Buffer::Instance` (for body), `TrailerMap`.\n- Decoder filters (request path) are invoked in **FIFO** order; encoder filters (response path) in **LIFO** order.\n- Filters return rich status enums (`FilterHeadersStatus`, `FilterDataStatus`, `FilterTrailersStatus`) with buffering and watermark control.\n- The terminal decoder filter is typically the **router filter**, which forwards requests upstream.\n\n### Why They Are Separate\n\nThe two filter chain levels exist because they operate at fundamentally different abstraction levels:\n\n1. **Scope and multiplexing**: A network filter chain is per-connection and handles raw byte streams. For HTTP/2 and HTTP/3, a single connection carries multiple concurrent streams. The HTTP filter chain is per-stream, allowing independent processing of each request/response pair within a multiplexed connection.\n\n2. **Protocol independence**: Network filters are protocol-agnostic. The same listener can handle TCP proxy traffic (no HTTP parsing) or HTTP traffic depending on which network filters are configured. The HTTP connection manager is itself a network filter that bridges the two levels.\n\n3. **Configuration flexibility**: Network-level filter chain selection uses connection properties available before any data is read (destination IP, SNI from TLS ClientHello, etc.). HTTP-level processing uses request-level properties (headers, routes, etc.) that are only available after HTTP parsing.\n\n### How They Relate\n\nThe relationship is hierarchical:\n\n```\nListener\n  -> FilterChainManager selects a Network::FilterChain (per connection)\n    -> Network::FilterManager runs network filters (per connection)\n      -> ConnectionManagerImpl (a network ReadFilter)\n        -> Codec parses HTTP frames\n          -> ActiveStream created (per HTTP stream)\n            -> Http::FilterManager runs HTTP filters (per stream)\n              -> Router filter (terminal) sends to upstream\n```\n\nThe `ConnectionManagerImpl` serves as the bridge: it is a `Network::ReadFilter` in the network filter chain, and it owns the HTTP codec and creates `Http::FilterManager` instances for each stream. Its `onData()` method receives raw bytes from the network filter pipeline, passes them to the HTTP codec for parsing, and the codec triggers HTTP-level processing through `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()`/`decodeData()`, which delegates to the per-stream `Http::FilterManager`.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Files and Classes\n\n| Component | File | Class/Function 1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Architecture

## Q1: Listener to Connection Manager

### Filter Chain Selection

When a downstream client opens a TCP connection, the listener first runs **listener filters** (e.g., TLS Inspector, HTTP Inspector) to populate connection metadata such as SNI, ALPN, and detected protocol. Once listener filters complete, `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` (`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:27`) is called.

This method invokes `FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()` (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.cc:542`) to select the appropriate network filter chain. The selection algorithm is a multi-level matching hierarchy:

1. **Destination port** — matches on the local port (or catch-all port 0)
2. **Destination IP** — matches on the local IP address via `findFilterChainForDestinationIP()` using a `LcTrie` for CIDR matching (`:591`)
3. **Server name (SNI)** — matches on exact server name, wildcard domains, or catch-all via `findFilterChainForServerName()` (`:608`)
4. **Transport protocol** — matches on detected transport protocol (e.g., `"tls"`) via `findFilterChainForTransportProtocol()` (`:639`)
5. **Application protocol (ALPN)** — matches on application protocols via `findFilterChainForApplicationProtocols()`

Alternatively, if a `matcher_` is configured (xDS filter chain matching), `findFilterChainUsingMatcher()` (`:577`) uses the Unified Matcher Framework instead.

If no filter chain matches, the connection is closed with `no_filter_chain_match` (`active_stream_listener_base.cc:31-40`). If a default filter chain is configured, it serves as fallback.

### Installing the HTTP Connection Manager

After selecting a `Network::FilterChain`, `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` calls `
